next generation <a href="/wiki/Business_class" title="Business class">Club World</a> seat. These seats are available on all of BA\'s wide-body aircraft, except the Airbus A350-1000 XWB.</div></div></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Short_haul">Short haul</span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_class">Economy class</span></h4>\n<p><i>Euro Traveller</i> is British Airways\' economy class cabin on all short-haul flights within Europe, including domestic flights within the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-ST_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ST-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\nHeathrow and Gatwick based flights are operated by Airbus A320 series aircraft. Standard seat pitch varies from 29" to 34" depending on aircraft type and location of the seat.\n</p><p>All flights from Heathrow and Gatwick have a <a href="/wiki/Buy_on_board" title="Buy on board">buy on board</a> system with a range of food provided by <a href="/wiki/Marks_and_Spencer" class="mw-redirect" title="Marks and Spencer">Marks and Spencer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>\nPurchases can only be made by using credit and debit card or by using Frequent Flyer Avios points.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> British Airways is rolling out Wi-Fi across its fleet of aircraft with 90% expected to be Wi-Fi enabled by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Scheduled services operated by <a href="/wiki/BA_Cityflyer" class="mw-redirect" title="BA Cityflyer">BA Cityflyer</a> currently offer complimentary onboard catering. The service will switch to buy on board in the future.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_class">Business class</span></h4>\n<p><i>Club Europe</i> is the short-haul business class available on all short-haul flights. This class allows for access to business lounges at most airports and complimentary onboard catering.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> The middle seat of the standard Airbus configured cabin is left free. Instead, a cocktail table folds up from under the middle seat on refurbished aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-BAP_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BAP-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> Pillows and blankets are available on longer flights.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/In-flight_entertainment" title="In-flight entertainment">In-flight</a> \n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mid-haul_and_long_haul">Mid-haul and long haul</span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="First_class">First class</span></h4>\n<p><i>First</i> is offered on all British Airways Airbus A380s, Boeing 777-300ERs, Boeing 787-9/10s and on some of their Boeing 777-200ERs. There are between eight and fourteen private suites depending on the aircraft type. Each First suit comes with a 6&#160;ft 6&#160;in (1.98&#160;m) bed, a 15-inch (38&#160;cm) wide entertainment screen, and in-seat power.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>\nDedicated British Airways \'Galleries First\' lounges are available at some airports. The exclusive \'Concorde Room\' lounges at Heathrow Terminal 5 and New York JFK airports offer pre-flight dining with waiter service and more intimate space. Business lounges are used where these are not available.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_World">Club World</span></h4>\n<p><i>Club World</i> is the mid-haul and long-haul <a href="/wiki/Business_class" title="Business class">business class</a> cabin. It is offered on all Boeing 777, Boeing 787, Airbus A318, Airbus A380, and selected Airbus A321 aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CWL_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CWL-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> The cabin features fully convertible flat bed seats. In 2006, British Airways launched <i>Next Generation New Club World</i>, featuring larger seats.<sup id="cite_ref-BAP_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BAP-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The Club World cabins are all configured in a similar design on widebody aircraft with aisle seats facing forwards, while middle seats and window seats face backwards (British Airways is one of only five carriers with backwards-facing business-class seats; American Airlines, <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Airways" title="Qatar Airways">Qatar Airways</a> are the others). \n</p><p>In March 2019, BA unveiled its new business-class seats on the new A350 aircraft, which feature a suite with a door.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> This will be re-fitted on to most of BAs wide-body fleet over the coming years.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Traveller_Plus">World Traveller Plus</span></h4>\n<p><i>World Traveller Plus</i> is the <a href="/wiki/Premium_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Premium economy">premium economy</a> class cabin provided on all BA long haul aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-ST_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ST-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> This cabin offers wider seats, extended leg-room, additional seat comforts such as larger IFE screen (on most aircraft) a foot rest and power sockets.<sup id="cite_ref-WTP_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WTP-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> A complimentary \'World Traveller\' bar is offered along with an upgraded main meal.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Traveller">World Traveller</span></h4>\n<p><i>World Traveller</i> is the mid-haul and long-haul economy class cabin. It offers seat-back entertainment, complimentary food and drink, pillows, and blankets.<sup id="cite_ref-ST_151-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ST-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WTNC_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WTNC-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> AVOD personal TV screens are available on all A321s, A350s, A380s, B777s and B787s.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> AC power outlets and USB plug-in points are offered in every seat row on the Airbus A350, A380, Boeing B787, B777-300ER and on refurbished B777-200ER aircraft. The outlets accept both UK and US plugs.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents_and_accidents">Incidents and accidents</span></h2>\n<p>British Airways is known to have a strong reputation for safety and has been consistently ranked within the top 20 safest airlines globally according to <i><a href="/wiki/Business_Insider" title="Business Insider">Business Insider</a></i> and <i>AirlineRatings.com.</i><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since BA\'s inception in 1974, it has been involved in three hull-loss incidents (<a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Flight_149" title="British Airways Flight 149">British Airways Flight 149</a> was destroyed on the ground at <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_International_Airport" title="Kuwait International Airport">Kuwait International Airport</a> as a result of military action during the <a href="/wiki/First_Gulf_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First Gulf War">First Gulf War</a> with no one on board) and two hijacking attempts. To date, the only fatal accident experienced by a BA aircraft occurred in 1976 with <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Flight_476" class="mw-redirect" title="British Airways Flight 476">British Airways Flight 476</a> which was involved in a midair collision later attributed to an error made by <a href="/wiki/Air_traffic_control" title="Air traffic control">air traffic control</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BA38_Crash.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/BA38_Crash.jpg/220px-BA38_Crash.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/BA38_Crash.jpg/330px-BA38_Crash.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/BA38_Crash.jpg/440px-BA38_Crash.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2896" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BA38_Crash.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The damaged British Airways Flight 38, photographed on 17 January 2008.</div></div></div>\n<ul><li>On 22 November 1974, British Airways Flight 870 was hijacked shortly after take-off from <a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Airport" title="Dubai International Airport">Dubai International Airport</a> for London-Heathrow. The <a href="/wiki/Vickers_VC10" title="Vickers VC10">Vickers VC10</a> landed at <a href="/wiki/Tripoli" title="Tripoli">Tripoli</a> for refuelling before flying on to Tunis. The captain, Jim Futcher, returned to the aircraft to fly it knowing the hijackers were on board. A hostage, 43-year-old German banker Werner Gustav Kehl, was shot in the back. The hijackers eventually surrendered after 84 hours. Futcher was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Gallantry_Medal" title="Queen&#39;s Gallantry Medal">Queen\'s Gallantry Medal</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Guild_of_Air_Pilots_and_Air_Navigators" class="mw-redirect" title="Guild of Air Pilots and Air Navigators">Guild of Air Pilots and Air Navigators</a> Founders Medal, the <a href="/wiki/British_Air_Line_Pilots_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="British Air Line Pilots Association">British Air Line Pilots Association</a> Gold Medal and a Certificate of Commendation from British Airways for his actions during the hijacking.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Medals_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Medals-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 10 September 1976, a <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Siddeley_Trident" title="Hawker Siddeley Trident">Trident 3B</a> on <a href="/wiki/1976_Zagreb_mid-air_collision" title="1976 Zagreb mid-air collision">British Airways Flight 476</a> departed from London-Heathrow to Istanbul. It collided in mid-air with an <a href="/wiki/Inex_Adria" class="mw-redirect" title="Inex Adria">Inex Adria</a> <a href="/wiki/McDonnell-Douglas_DC-9" class="mw-redirect" title="McDonnell-Douglas DC-9">DC9-31</a> near <a href="/wiki/Zagreb" title="Zagreb">Zagreb</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> All 54 passengers and 9 crew members on the BA aircraft died. This is the only fatal accident to a British Airways aircraft since the company\'s formation in 1974.</li>\n<li>On 24 June 1982, <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Flight_9" title="British Airways Flight 9">British Airways Flight 9</a>, a Boeing 747-200 registration <i>G-BDXH</i>, flew through a cloud of volcanic ash and dust from the eruption of <a href="/wiki/Galunggung" title="Galunggung">Mount Galunggung</a>. The ash and dust caused extensive damage to the aircraft, including the failure of all four engines.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> The crew managed to glide the plane out of the dust cloud and restart all four of its engines, although one later had to be shut down again. The volcanic ash caused the cockpit window to be scratched to such an extent that it was difficult for the pilots to see out of the plane. However, the aircraft made a successful emergency landing at <a href="/wiki/Halim_Perdanakusuma_International_Airport" title="Halim Perdanakusuma International Airport">Halim Perdanakusuma International Airport</a> just outside <a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a>. There were no fatalities or injuries.<sup id="cite_ref-Black_Box_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Black_Box-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 10 June 1990, <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Flight_5390" title="British Airways Flight 5390">British Airways Flight 5390</a>, a <a href="/wiki/BAC_One-Eleven" title="BAC One-Eleven">BAC One-Eleven</a> flight between <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a> and <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga" title="M\xc3\xa1laga">M\xc3\xa1laga</a>, suffered a windscreen blowout due to the fitting of incorrect bolts the previous day. The captain suffered major injuries after being partially blown out of the aircraft, but the co-pilot landed the plane safely at <a href="/wiki/Southampton_Airport" title="Southampton Airport">Southampton Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-OgdenInterview_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OgdenInterview-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 2 August 1990, <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Flight_149" title="British Airways Flight 149">British Airways Flight 149</a> landed at <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_International_Airport" title="Kuwait International Airport">Kuwait International Airport</a> four hours after the Iraqi invasion of <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>. The aircraft, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747-100</a> <i>G-AWND</i>, was destroyed, and all passengers and crew were captured. Two of the landing gears were salvaged, and are on display in Waterside, BA Headquarters in London.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 29 December 2000, <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Flight_2069" title="British Airways Flight 2069">British Airways Flight 2069</a> was en route from London to Nairobi when a mentally ill passenger entered the cockpit and grabbed the controls. As the pilots struggled to remove the intruder, the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400</a> stalled twice and banked to 94 degrees. Several people on board were injured by the violent manoeuvres, which briefly caused the aircraft to descend at 30,000&#160;ft per minute<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. The man was finally restrained with the help of several passengers, and the co-pilot regained control of the aircraft. The flight landed safely in Nairobi.</li>\n<li>On 17 January 2008, <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Flight_38" title="British Airways Flight 38">British Airways Flight 38</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777" title="Boeing 777">Boeing 777-200ER</a> <i>G-YMMM</i>, from <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Capital_International_Airport" title="Beijing Capital International Airport">Beijing</a> to London crash-landed approximately 1,000 feet (300&#160;m) short of Heathrow Airport\'s runway 27L, and slid onto the runway\'s <a href="/wiki/Displaced_threshold" title="Displaced threshold">displaced threshold</a>. The aircraft sustained damage to its landing gear, wing roots, and engines, resulting in the first hull loss of a Boeing 777. There were no fatalities, but there was one serious injury and 12 minor injuries. The accident was caused by icing in the fuel system, resulting in a loss of power.</li>\n<li>On 24 May 2013, British Airways Flight 762, using an <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319-131" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A319-131">Airbus A319-131</a> and registered as G-EUOE, returned to Heathrow Airport after fan cowl doors detached from both engines shortly after takeoff. During the approach, a fire broke out in the right engine and persisted after the engine was shut down. The aircraft landed safely with no injuries to the 80 people on board. A preliminary accident report revealed that the cowlings had been left unlatched following overnight maintenance. The separation of the doors caused airframe damage and the right-hand engine fire resulted from a ruptured fuel pipe.</li>\n<li>On 22 December 2013, British Airways Flight 34, a Boeing 747-436 <i>G-BNLL</i>, hit a building at <a href="/wiki/O._R._Tambo_International_Airport" title="O. R. Tambo International Airport">O. R. Tambo International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a> after missing a turning on a taxiway. The starboard wing was severely damaged but there were no injuries amongst the crew or 189 passengers, however, four members of ground staff were injured when the wing smashed into the building.<sup id="cite_ref-Tel10534084_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tel10534084-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> The aircraft was officially withdrawn from service in February 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-BASourceBNLL_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BASourceBNLL-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 8 September 2015, <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Flight_2276" title="British Airways Flight 2276">British Airways Flight 2276</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 777-200">Boeing 777-236ER</a> <i>G-VIIO</i>, aborted its takeoff at <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas</a>\' <a href="/wiki/McCarran_International_Airport" title="McCarran International Airport">McCarran International Airport</a> due to an <a href="/wiki/Uncontained_engine_failure" class="mw-redirect" title="Uncontained engine failure">uncontained engine failure</a><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> of its left (<a href="/wiki/Aircraft_engine_position_number" class="mw-redirect" title="Aircraft engine position number">#1</a>) <a href="/wiki/General_Electric_GE90" title="General Electric GE90">General Electric GE90</a> engine, which led to a substantial fire. The aircraft was evacuated on the main runway. All 157 passengers and 13 crew escaped the aircraft, at least 14 people sustaining minor injuries.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Between 21 August 2018 and 5 September 2018, hackers carried out a "sophisticated, malicious criminal attack" on the website of the airline. Around 380,000 transactions were affected by this <a href="/wiki/Web_skimming" title="Web skimming">web skimming</a> attack.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> The company was subsequently fined \xc2\xa3183 million (1.5% of turnover) in July 2019, by the <a href="/wiki/Information_Commissioner%27s_Office" title="Information Commissioner&#39;s Office">Information Commissioner\'s Office</a>, the highest ever fine handed by the ICO at the time of issuing.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Air_transport_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Air
